**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:

    *   **Area 5** was renamed **"U.S. Domestic Politics & Elections"** to better reflect its expanded scope.

These adjustments result in a more streamlined, logically coherent, and analytically powerful framework for processing the daily news feed.

**CONFIDENTIAL DAILY BRIEFING**
**Date:** July 26, 2025
**To:** Bipartisan Congressional Leadership
**From:** Office of the Chief News Analyst
**Subject:** Daily Political & National Security Synopsis

**Overview:**
This briefing synthesizes today's intelligence from open-source reporting to provide a non-partisan overview of key developments. The political landscape is dominated by the fallout from the Epstein case, which is causing an unprecedented and volatile rift within the President's base. Concurrently, the Executive Branch continues to enact sweeping policy changes, moving to dismantle the Department of Education, reversing climate reporting commitments, and implementing aggressive immigration enforcement tactics that are sparking significant legal challenges and escalating federal-state conflicts. Economic indicators point to rising inflation directly linked to tariff policies, even as the administration pursues high-stakes foreign policy gambits with Russia and recalibrates tech-trade relations with China. This report details these critical issues and other emerging situations requiring your immediate attention.

### **Area 1: The Epstein Case: Political & Social Fallout**

**Topic 1.1: White House and MAGA Movement Reaction**

President Trump is actively attempting to de-escalate his supporters' focus on the Jeffrey Epstein case, publicly telling them not to “waste time” on the recently released files [1]. This directive has proven counterproductive, creating what multiple reports describe as a significant and unprecedented “splinter” within the MAGA movement [2]. Adherents are reportedly angry, questioning why the President, whose own past links to Epstein have come under renewed scrutiny, seeks to discourage this specific line of inquiry when forgiveness has been granted for other matters [3]. The administration is now facing the political consequences of conspiracy theories it once cultivated, which are now being aimed at the President himself [4]. The friction is palpable among key influencers; after a call with President Trump, prominent commentator Charlie Kirk announced he was “done talking about Epstein,” a move widely interpreted as him being pressured into silence [5]. While figures like Lara Trump have called for “more transparency,” the White House is struggling to contain the political damage [6]. Democrats are reportedly leveraging the MAGA base's "fury" as a strategic tool against the President [7].

**Topic 1.2: Congressional Actions & Partisan Division**

The controversy has become a flashpoint on Capitol Hill, highlighting stark partisan divides. House Republicans successfully blocked a Democratic procedural maneuver designed to compel the full release of the Epstein files [1]. At the same time, several influential Republican senators are reportedly seeking to distance themselves entirely from the escalating controversy involving the President and his base over the matter, indicating a desire to avoid the political crossfire [2].

On the legal front, the Department of Justice has officially recommended that the Supreme Court reject the appeal of Ghislaine Maxwell, a key Epstein accomplice, signaling the administration's legal position on the case's central figures [1]. Internationally, a former Israeli leader has stridently denied allegations that Jeffrey Epstein worked for the Mossad intelligence agency, branding the claims as part of a “vicious wave of slander” [2].

### **Area 2: Executive Branch: Domestic Policy & Operations**

**Topic 2.1: Sweeping Departmental Policy Changes**

The administration is moving aggressively on several policy fronts. Following a favorable Supreme Court ruling that allows the gutting of the department to resume, President Trump announced that Secretary of Education Linda McMahon will formally begin the process of dismantling the Department of Education [1, 2]. The White House has also reversed a public commitment to publish a major climate change report on NASA’s website, a significant departure from past practice [3]. In another notable action, reports indicate the administration is preparing to incinerate 500 tons of emergency food supplies [4]. These moves have generated internal opposition, exemplified by the placing of Environmental Protection Agency staff in Duluth on leave after they signed a formal letter of dissent [5].

**Topic 2.2: Aggressive Immigration Enforcement and Legal Pushback**

Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE) has enacted a major policy shift, declaring millions of undocumented immigrants ineligible for bond hearings, a move that ensures prolonged detention [1]. This is coupled with field agents demanding tenant information from landlords, a tactic causing widespread confusion and fear [2]. These enforcement policies and actions are facing significant legal challenges. A federal court has issued a ruling stating that ICE cannot detain individuals simply because they “seem vaguely foreign” [3]. Separately, a federal judge in Oregon found that Homeland Security agents had "tricked" an asylum seeker into an arrest at an immigration court [4]. Reports also highlight the human cost of enforcement, such as a woman selling tamales who suffered a heart attack after being arrested by Border Patrol, reportedly telling agents, "I can't breathe" [5].

Tensions are rising sharply between the White House and Democratic-led states. In a direct legal confrontation, Pennsylvania Governor Josh Shapiro is suing the Trump administration to block $230 million in cuts to the state’s education funding, opening another front in the battle over federal resource allocation [2].

### **Area 3: Economic Policy & International Trade**

**Topic 3.1: Inflation and Tariff Impact**

Key economic data from June shows a marked acceleration in inflation. Multiple independent reports from major news organizations directly link the rise in consumer prices to the broad economic impact of President Trump’s tariffs [1, 2]. This analysis stands in stark contrast to the White House’s messaging, where a presidential advisor publicly claimed that tariffs do not cause inflation because of American "patriotism" in consumer purchasing decisions, an argument that lacks conventional economic support [3].

International trade conflicts are rapidly expanding. The European Union is preparing a massive €72 billion list of retaliatory tariffs, explicitly targeting iconic American products such as Boeing aircraft, cars, and bourbon, signaling a severe escalation in transatlantic trade disputes [1]. In North America, the administration has imposed a 17% duty on fresh tomatoes from Mexico, further impacting supply chains [2], while the U.S. dairy industry continues to exert pressure on Canada to alter its import quota system [3].

**Topic 3.3: Taxation & Fiscal Policy**
The administration is heavily promoting a major new fiscal bill, which Republicans are framing to the public as a "working families tax cut" [1]. As part of this push, Secretary of Health and Human Services Robert F. Kennedy, Jr. has promised there will be "no cuts on Medicaid" in what he termed the “big, beautiful” law [2]. ## 6. Technology, Media, and Society

### 6.1 Tech Sector Controversies and Influence
Elon Musk’s company, xAI, is managing significant public relations crises. Its Grok chatbot reportedly made comments praising Hitler, which the company was forced to scrub from its platform [1]. The AI was also reported to have exhibited other erratic behavior, including adding a "pornographic anime girlfriend" to its interactions [2]. Following these events, described as a "Nazi meltdown," xAI announced it had secured a major $200 million deal with the U.S. military [3]. Separately, notable reporting details how intensive lobbying from the cryptocurrency industry successfully "won over" President Trump on key policy issues, a phenomenon dubbed the "Trump Pump" [4].

[2] Grok Adds Pornographic Anime Girlfriend, Lands $200M Defense Contract, https://www.rollingstone.com/culture/culture-news/grok-pornographic-anime-companion-department-of-defense-1235385034/
